<Rating>5</Rating>< Text>
Lived here for 4 years with a young family (2 kids), in a 2 BR/2 BA unit.  Had one of the "classic" (30-year-old, pre-renovation) units.  We felt it was a fair price and a fair value for a family. < Text>
Pros: I lived here for 10 months towards the end of my time in the Marines. IMT Sorrento Valley was a pretty good place to live for the price, in SoCal that is. Tayla and Ivan in the office are extremely polite and professional, we had nothing but great interactions with them. The amenities were small but well maintained, having five pools to choose from was awesome! At the time only having one gym was a bit of an issue BUT I know that they've started working on putting a few more gyms in the complex and they are open 24/7. The Nest smart thermostats are amazing as well!

Cons: The newly renovated apartments have a vinyl flooring was uneven in some spots causing my wife's office chair to spin on its own! This was considered regular wear and tear and we were not charged for it. The paint on the walls is a bit cheap and we had some chipping issues, we owed them some money in the end to repaint the walls. The maintenance workers did their job will but we did have an issue with maintenance workers entering our apartment unexpectedly without notice due to a mix-up at the leasing office. We were not home at the time and got a call from SimpliSafe (which we were allowed to install, due to the fact it all command strips up and didn't require drilling, etc.). Due to the alarm tripping and the San Diego police responding, we also received a call from the leasing office.

All in all, our experience here was for sure a 4 out of 5. We received 65% of our security deposit back.</Text>

<Text>In three years with Uncut, this is my assessment. Yours is probably gonna be different.

As far as calling services perform, this ranks highly among the best for your money and results. Nearly all calling services charge you monthly rates. Some charge yearly rates. Uncut offers a one time lifetime membership fee provided you

- Update your availability weekly (easy)
- show yourself accountable & reliable

In my experience, the following impact the amount of work you book:

DIRECTLY:
‚Ä¢ Your look and skill set
‚Ä¢  the level of demand for them for relevant productions
‚Ä¢ the level of reliability of your transportation
‚Ä¢ the number of locations/regions of L.A. you're willing to travel to
‚Ä¢ your conduct on set and off

After this, there's the matter of choosing the plan that works best for your station at the station of life you're in.

‚Ä¢ First, of all, is doing what we can do the best we can. Update your availability weekly and show up early regularly and be easy to work with.

Anticipate traffic delays and plan the safest and quickest ways ahead to make your call time at least ten to fifteen minutes early in order to avoid causing production delays in your end.
Uncut is on your side provided you keep the communication lines with them open and reach them ASAP..

CHOOSING A PLAN:
Skip the Silver membership as it is a waste of your time and money. Non union actors do best with the Gold membership at $150 for the whole year.
While I've heard that other calling services book more work for a lot more money,
Uncut anticipates lulls between seasons.
Jacques, its founder and manager since 2001, offers loyal clients a lifetime* membership as a way of expressing his thanks for staying with them.

Save the Platinum for when you go Union, as Uncut will send you on auditions they feel you may be right for with this.

FINAL  THOUGHTS:
Give Uncut at least a year as a Gold level member before giving them a final weigh-in.

Nice store! Very clean, great variety, and a bomb selection of deli foods. They've got a station for rice bowls and sushi, fried chicken, deli meats, sandwich station, bakery and caf√®. Like seriously, what more you asking for!?
My husband gets the sushi often and it is actually pretty good. Definitely one of the best we've had for grocery store variety. It is moderately priced as well - I've never seen a combo priced above twelve dollars. Tastier and slightly less expensive than Safeway.

Bel Air is not where I go for groceries normally, though. As you can imagine, while the food is typically good quality, it does not have the most affordable prices. < review>
I love this Bel Air supermarket. Nothing beats the service here!

It's always so clean and the employees go out of their way to make sure you have a pleasant shopping experience.

Price-wise, it really does depend what you're after. If you pay attention to the sales that are going on, you can get items a lot cheaper than elsewhere. Like for me, my favorite cereal is Barbara's Peanut Butter Puffins. Now these boxes of crunchy pseudo-Captain Crunch pillows go for about $4 on average. Sometimes I can get them for $2.50 a box. Score!

Parking is easy and the fact that you can always count on some healthy young person to cart your grocery shopping to your car is a plus.<//review>
